.navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Physical_cosmology" title="Template:Physical cosmology"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Physical_cosmology" title="Template talk:Physical cosmology"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Physical_cosmology&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Albert Einstein</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">EYEN</span>-styne</i></a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NDxay_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-NDxay-7">[6]</a></sup> <small>German: </small><span class="IPA" lang="de-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈalbɛʁt ˈʔaɪnʃtaɪn]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_german.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/De-Albert_Einstein.oga" title="De-Albert Einstein.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; 14 March 1879 – 18 April 1955) was a German-born <a href="/wiki/Theoretical_physics" title="Theoretical physics">theoretical physicist</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bio-8">[7]</a></sup> with Switzerland and the United States citizenships, widely acknowledged to be one of the greatest and most influential physicists of all time. Einstein is best known for developing the <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_relativity" title="Theory of relativity">theory of relativity</a>, but he also made important contributions to the development of the theory of <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>. Relativity and quantum mechanics are together the two pillars of <a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">modern physics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-frs-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YangHamilton2010_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-YangHamilton2010-9">[8]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass–energy equivalence">mass–energy equivalence</a> formula <span class="texhtml"><a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence#Mass–velocity_relationship" title="Mass–energy equivalence"><i>E</i> = <i>mc</i><sup>2</sup></a></span>, which arises from relativity theory, has been dubbed "the world's most famous equation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LnLVo_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-LnLVo-10">[9]</a></sup> His work is also known for its influence on the <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_science" title="Philosophy of science">philosophy of science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xZQWt_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-xZQWt-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3UiiT_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-3UiiT-12">[11]</a></sup> He received the 1921 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> "for his services to theoretical physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the <a href="/wiki/Photoelectric_effect" title="Photoelectric effect">photoelectric effect</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-13">[12]</a></sup> a pivotal step in the development of quantum theory. His intellectual achievements and originality resulted in "Einstein" becoming synonymous with "genius".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wordnetweb.princeton.edu_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-wordnetweb.princeton.edu-14">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1905, a year sometimes described as his <i><a href="/wiki/Annus_mirabilis" title="Annus mirabilis">annus mirabilis</a></i> ('miracle year'), Einstein published <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers">four groundbreaking papers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377-15">[14]</a></sup> These outlined the theory of the photoelectric effect, explained <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, introduced <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>, and demonstrated mass-energy equivalence. Einstein thought that the laws of <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical mechanics</a> could no longer be reconciled with those of the <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_field" title="Electromagnetic field">electromagnetic field</a>, which led him to develop his special theory of relativity. He then extended the theory to gravitational fields; he published a paper on <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> in 1916, introducing his theory of gravitation. In 1917, he applied the general theory of relativity to model the structure of the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151124_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151124-17">[16]</a></sup> He continued to deal with problems of <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">statistical mechanics</a> and quantum theory, which led to his explanations of particle theory and the <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">motion of molecules</a>. He also investigated the thermal properties of light and the quantum theory of <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a>, which laid the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photon</a> theory of light.
</p><p>However, for much of the later part of his career, he worked on two ultimately unsuccessful endeavors. First, despite his great contributions to quantum mechanics, he opposed what it evolved into, objecting that "God does not play dice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Second, he attempted to devise a <a href="/wiki/Unified_field_theory" title="Unified field theory">unified field theory</a> by generalizing his geometric theory of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitation" title="Gravitation">gravitation</a> to include <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">electromagnetism</a>. As a result, he became increasingly isolated from the mainstream of modern <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>.
</p><p>Einstein was born in the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, but moved to <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> in 1895, forsaking his German citizenship (as a subject of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Kingdom of Württemberg">Kingdom of Württemberg</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GEcitizen_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-GEcitizen-1">[note 1]</a></sup> the following year. In 1897, at the age of 17, he enrolled in the mathematics and physics teaching diploma program at the Swiss <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">Federal polytechnic school</a> in <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, graduating in 1900. In 1901, he acquired Swiss citizenship, which he kept for the rest of his life, and in 1903 he secured a permanent position at the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Institute_of_Intellectual_Property" title="Swiss Federal Institute of Intellectual Property">Swiss Patent Office</a> in Bern. In 1905, he was awarded a PhD by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Zurich" title="University of Zurich">University of Zurich</a>. In 1914, Einstein moved to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in order to join the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Prussian Academy of Sciences">Prussian Academy of Sciences</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a>. In 1917, Einstein became director of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Institute_for_Physics" title="Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics">Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics</a>; he also became a German citizen again, this time <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a>.
</p><p>In 1933, while Einstein was visiting the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> came to power in Germany. Einstein, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>, objected to the policies of the newly elected <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi government</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zE9Bz_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-zE9Bz-19">[18]</a></sup> he settled in the United States and became an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_citizen" title="American citizen">American citizen</a> in 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoyerDubofsky2001_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoyerDubofsky2001-20">[19]</a></sup> On the eve of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, he endorsed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szil%C3%A1rd_letter" title="Einstein–Szilárd letter">a letter</a> to President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> alerting him to the potential <a href="/wiki/German_nuclear_weapons_program" title="German nuclear weapons program">German nuclear weapons program</a> and recommending that the US begin <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">similar research</a>. Einstein supported the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> but generally denounced the idea of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Einstein_family" title="Einstein family">Einstein family</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_(1882).jpg"><img alt="A young boy with short hair and a round face, wearing a white collar and large bow, with vest, coat, skirt, and high boots. He is leaning against an ornate chair." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="414" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_(1882).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Einstein at the age of three in 1882</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg"><img alt="Studio photo of a boy seated in a relaxed posture and wearing a suit, posed in front of a backdrop of scenery." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="379" decoding="async" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein in 1893 (age 14)</div></div></div>
<p>Albert Einstein was born in <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bio-8">[7]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Kingdom of Württemberg">Kingdom of Württemberg</a> in the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, on 14 March 1879 into a family of secular <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> His parents were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hermann_Einstein" title="Hermann Einstein">Hermann Einstein</a>, a salesman and engineer, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pauline_Koch" title="Pauline Koch">Pauline Koch</a>. In 1880, the family moved to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, where Einstein's father and his uncle Jakob founded <i>Elektrotechnische Fabrik J. Einstein &amp; Cie</i>, a company that manufactured electrical equipment based on <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bio-8">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Albert attended a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_school" title="Catholic school">Catholic elementary school</a> in Munich, from the age of five, for three years. At the age of eight, he was transferred to the Luitpold-Gymnasium (now known as the Albert-Einstein-Gymnasium), where he received advanced primary and secondary school education until he left the German Empire seven years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA59_59–61]_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA59_59–61]-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1894, Hermann and Jakob's company lost a bid to supply the city of Munich with electrical lighting because they lacked the capital to convert their equipment from the <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) standard to the more efficient <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC) standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EQyag_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-EQyag-24">[23]</a></sup> The loss forced the sale of the Munich factory. In search of business, the Einstein family moved to Italy, first to <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and a few months later to <a href="/wiki/Pavia" title="Pavia">Pavia</a>. When the family moved to Pavia, Einstein, then 15, stayed in Munich to finish his studies at the Luitpold Gymnasium. His father intended for him to pursue <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, but Einstein clashed with the authorities and resented the school's regimen and teaching method. He later wrote that the spirit of learning and creative thought was lost in strict <a href="/wiki/Rote_learning" title="Rote learning">rote learning</a>. At the end of December 1894, he traveled to Italy to join his family in Pavia, convincing the school to let him go by using a doctor's note.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199730–31_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199730–31-25">[24]</a></sup> During his time in Italy he wrote a short essay with the title "On the Investigation of the State of the <a href="/wiki/Aether_(classical_element)" title="Aether (classical element)">Ether</a> in a Magnetic Field".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._5_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._5-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1RgTv_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-1RgTv-27">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein excelled at math and physics from a young age, reaching a mathematical level years ahead of his peers. The 12-year-old Einstein taught himself algebra and Euclidean geometry over a single summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Einstein also independently discovered his own original proof of the <a href="/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem" title="Pythagorean theorem">Pythagorean theorem</a> aged 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FVfDU_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FVfDU-29">[28]</a></sup> A family tutor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Max_Talmud" title="Max Talmud">Max Talmud</a> says that after he had given the 12-year-old Einstein a geometry textbook, after a short time "[Einstein] had worked through the whole book. He thereupon devoted himself to higher mathematics... Soon the flight of his mathematical genius was so high I could not follow."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717-30">[29]</a></sup> His passion for geometry and algebra led the 12-year-old to become convinced that nature could be understood as a "mathematical structure".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717-30">[29]</a></sup> Einstein started teaching himself calculus at 12, and as a 14-year-old he says he had "mastered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integral_calculus" title="Integral calculus">integral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Differential_calculus" title="Differential calculus">differential calculus</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200716_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200716-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the age of 13, when he had become more seriously interested in philosophy (and music),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe20058_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe20058-32">[31]</a></sup> Einstein was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Kant</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Critique_of_Pure_Reason" title="Critique of Pure Reason">Critique of Pure Reason</a></i>. Kant became his favorite philosopher, his tutor stating: "At the time he was still a child, only thirteen years old, yet Kant's works, incomprehensible to ordinary mortals, seemed to be clear to him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200717-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_(color2).jpg"><img alt="Einstein's matriculation certificate at the age of 17. The heading translates as &quot;The Education Committee of the Canton of Aargau&quot;. His scores were German 5, French 3, Italian 5, History 6, Geography 4, Algebra 6, Geometry 6, Descriptive Geometry 6, Physics 6, Chemistry 5, Natural History 5, Art Drawing 4, Technical Drawing 4. 6 = very good, 5 = good, 4 = sufficient, 3 = insufficient, 2 = poor, 1 = very poor." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2419" data-file-width="1479" decoding="async" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_(color2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Einstein's <i><a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">Matura</a></i> certificate, 1896<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MaturaScore_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-MaturaScore-33">[note 2]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 1895, at the age of 16, Einstein took the entrance examinations for the Swiss <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">Federal polytechnic school</a> in <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a> (later the Eidgenössische Technische Hochschule, ETH). He failed to reach the required standard in the general part of the examination,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_p._11_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_p._11-34">[32]</a></sup> but obtained exceptional grades in physics and mathematics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199736–37_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199736–37-35">[33]</a></sup> On the advice of the principal of the polytechnic school, he attended the <a href="/wiki/Old_Cantonal_School_Aarau" title="Old Cantonal School Aarau">Argovian cantonal school</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)"><i>gymnasium</i></a>) in <a href="/wiki/Aarau" title="Aarau">Aarau</a>, Switzerland, in 1895 and 1896 to complete his secondary schooling. While lodging with the family of <a href="/wiki/Jost_Winteler" title="Jost Winteler">Jost Winteler</a>, he fell in love with Winteler's daughter, Marie. Albert's sister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maja_Einstein" title="Maja Einstein">Maja</a> later married Winteler's son Paul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57-36">[34]</a></sup> In January 1896, with his father's approval, Einstein renounced his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_citizenship" title="German citizenship">citizenship in the German Kingdom of Württemberg</a> to avoid <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Germany" title="Conscription in Germany">military service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199740_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199740-37">[35]</a></sup> In September 1896 he passed the Swiss <i><a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">Matura</a></i> with mostly good grades, including a top grade of 6 in physics and mathematical subjects, on <a href="/wiki/Grading_systems_by_country#Switzerland" title="Grading systems by country">a scale of 1–6</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_docs._21–27_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_docs._21–27-38">[36]</a></sup> At 17, he enrolled in the four-year mathematics and physics teaching diploma program at the Federal polytechnic school. Marie Winteler, who was a year older, moved to <a href="/wiki/Olsberg,_Aargau" title="Olsberg, Aargau">Olsberg</a>, Switzerland, for a teaching post.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein's future wife, a 20-year-old <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbian</a> named <a href="/wiki/Mileva_Mari%C4%87" title="Mileva Marić">Mileva Marić</a>, also enrolled at the polytechnic school that year. She was the only woman among the six students in the mathematics and physics section of the teaching diploma course. Over the next few years, Einstein's and Marić's friendship developed into a romance, and they spent countless hours debating and reading books together on extra-curricular physics in which they were both interested. Einstein wrote in his letters to Marić that he preferred studying alongside her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mileva_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-mileva-39">[37]</a></sup> In 1900, Einstein passed the exams in Maths and Physics and was awarded a Federal teaching diploma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._67_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel_et_al.2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._67-40">[38]</a></sup> There is eyewitness evidence and several letters over many years that indicate Marić might have collaborated with Einstein prior to his landmark 1905 papers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mileva_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-mileva-39">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7HA7H_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-7HA7H-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1zJdH_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-1zJdH-42">[40]</a></sup> known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers"><i>Annus Mirabilis</i> papers</a>, and that they developed some of the concepts together during their studies, although some historians of physics who have studied the issue disagree that she made any substantive contributions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPais19941–29_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais19941–29-43">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xKrMG_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-xKrMG-44">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA49_49–56]_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA49_49–56]-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dUxMl_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-dUxMl-46">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages_and_children">Marriages and children</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2300" data-file-width="3324" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg/220px-Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg/330px-Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg/440px-Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_his_wife_Mileva_Maric.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein and <a href="/wiki/Mileva_Mari%C4%87" title="Mileva Marić">Mileva Marić</a> Einstein, 1912</div></div></div>
<p>Early correspondence between Einstein and Marić was discovered and published in 1987 which revealed that the couple had a daughter named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieserl_Einstein" title="Lieserl Einstein">"Lieserl"</a>, born in early 1902 in <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a> where Marić was staying with her parents. Marić returned to Switzerland without the child, whose real name and fate are unknown. The contents of Einstein's letter in September 1903 suggest that the girl was either given up for adoption or died of <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_fever" title="Scarlet fever">scarlet fever</a> in infancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBMes_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-HBMes-47">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe200522–23_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe200522–23-48">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein and Marić married in January 1903. In May 1904, their son <a href="/wiki/Hans_Albert_Einstein" title="Hans Albert Einstein">Hans Albert Einstein</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a>, Switzerland. Their son <a href="/wiki/Einstein_family#Eduard_&quot;Tete&quot;_Einstein_(Albert's_second_son)" title="Einstein family">Eduard</a> was born in Zürich in July 1910. The couple moved to Berlin in April 1914, but Marić returned to Zürich with their sons after learning that, despite their close relationship before,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mileva_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-mileva-39">[37]</a></sup> Einstein's chief romantic attraction was now his cousin <a href="/wiki/Elsa_Einstein" title="Elsa Einstein">Elsa Löwenthal</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel1966_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel1966-49">[47]</a></sup> she was his first cousin maternally and second cousin paternally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPA50_50]_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPA50_50]-50">[48]</a></sup> Einstein and Marić divorced on 14 February 1919, having lived apart for five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA50_50]_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidOAsQ_hFjhrACpgPA50_50]-52">[50]</a></sup> As part of the divorce settlement, Einstein agreed to give Marić any future (in the event, 1921) Nobel Prize money.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>In letters revealed in 2015, Einstein wrote to his early love Marie Winteler about his marriage and his strong feelings for her. He wrote in 1910, while his wife was pregnant with their second child: "I think of you in heartfelt love every spare minute and am so unhappy as only a man can be." He spoke about a "misguided love" and a "missed life" regarding his love for Marie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MlQLY_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-MlQLY-54">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein married Löwenthal in 1919,<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_November_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(November_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_55-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_November_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(November_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-55'>[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceKennefickSchulmann201562_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceKennefickSchulmann201562-56">[54]</a></sup> after having had a relationship with her since 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPA50_50]_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPA50_50]-50">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-dh-57">[55]</a></sup> They emigrated to the United States in 1933. Elsa was diagnosed with heart and kidney problems in 1935 and died in December 1936.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter1993216_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter1993216-58">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1923, Einstein fell in love with a secretary named Betty Neumann, the niece of a close friend, Hans Mühsam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> In a volume of letters released by <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem" title="Hebrew University of Jerusalem">Hebrew University of Jerusalem</a> in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> Einstein described about six women, including Margarete Lebach (a blonde Austrian), Estella Katzenellenbogen (the rich owner of a florist business), Toni Mendel (a wealthy Jewish widow) and Ethel Michanowski (a Berlin socialite), with whom he spent time and from whom he received gifts while being married to Elsa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Later, after the death of his second wife Elsa, Einstein was briefly in a relationship with Margarita Konenkova.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Konenkova was a Russian spy who was married to the noted Russian sculptor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Konenkov" title="Sergei Konenkov">Sergei Konenkov</a> (who created the bronze bust of Einstein at the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study" title="Institute for Advanced Study">Institute for Advanced Study</a> at Princeton).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein's son Eduard had a breakdown at about age 20 and was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson2015a_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson2015a-69">[67]</a></sup> His mother cared for him and he was also committed to asylums for several periods, finally, after her death, being committed permanently to <a href="/wiki/Burgh%C3%B6lzli" title="Burghölzli">Burghölzli</a>, the Psychiatric University Hospital in Zürich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeffe2007[httpsarchiveorgdetailseinsteinbiograph00neffpage203_203]_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeffe2007[httpsarchiveorgdetailseinsteinbiograph00neffpage203_203]-70">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patent_office">Patent office</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_patentoffice.jpg"><img alt="Head and shoulders shot of a young, moustached man with dark, curly hair wearing a plaid suit and vest, striped shirt, and a dark tie." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="870" data-file-width="666" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/170px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/255px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/340px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_patentoffice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Einstein in 1904 (age 25)</div></div></div>
<p>After graduating in 1900, Einstein spent almost two years searching for a teaching post. He acquired <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> citizenship in February 1901,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199782_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199782-71">[69]</a></sup> but was not <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Switzerland" title="Conscription in Switzerland">conscripted</a> for medical reasons. With the help of <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann" title="Marcel Grossmann">Marcel Grossmann</a>'s father, he secured a job in <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Institute_of_Intellectual_Property" title="Swiss Federal Institute of Intellectual Property">Swiss Patent Office</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODY5p_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODY5p-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200763_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200763-73">[71]</a></sup> as an <a href="/wiki/Patent_examiner" title="Patent examiner">assistant examiner – level III</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MeZPN_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-MeZPN-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGEFAQ_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGEFAQ-75">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein evaluated <a href="/wiki/Patent_application" title="Patent application">patent applications</a> for a variety of devices including a gravel sorter and an electromechanical typewriter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGEFAQ_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-IGEFAQ-75">[73]</a></sup> In 1903, his position at the Swiss Patent Office became permanent, although he was passed over for promotion until he "fully mastered machine technology".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalison2000370_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000370-76">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Much of his work at the patent office related to questions about transmission of electric signals and electrical-mechanical synchronization of time, two technical problems that show up conspicuously in the <a href="/wiki/Einstein%27s_thought_experiments" title="Einstein's thought experiments">thought experiments</a> that eventually led Einstein to his radical conclusions about the nature of light and the fundamental connection between space and time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalison2000377-15">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg"><img alt="Three young men in suits with high white collars and bow ties, sitting." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3066" data-file-width="4672" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/230px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/345px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/460px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympia_Academy" title="Olympia Academy">Olympia Academy</a> founders: <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Habicht" title="Conrad Habicht">Conrad Habicht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Solovine" title="Maurice Solovine">Maurice Solovine</a> and  Albert Einstein</div></div></div>
<p>With a few friends he had met in Bern, Einstein started a small discussion group in 1902, self-mockingly named "<a href="/wiki/Olympia_Academy" title="Olympia Academy">The Olympia Academy</a>", which met regularly to discuss science and philosophy. Sometimes they were joined by Mileva who attentively listened but did not participate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199396–98_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199396–98-77">[75]</a></sup> Their readings included the works of <a href="/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9" title="Henri Poincaré">Henri Poincaré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Mach" title="Ernst Mach">Ernst Mach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">David Hume</a>, which influenced his scientific and philosophical outlook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200779–84_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200779–84-78">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_scientific_papers">First scientific papers</span></h3>
<p>In 1900, Einstein's paper <a href="/wiki/List_of_scientific_publications_by_Albert_Einstein#Journal_articles" title="List of scientific publications by Albert Einstein">"Folgerungen aus den Capillaritätserscheinungen"</a> ("Conclusions from the Capillarity Phenomena") was published in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Annalen_der_Physik" title="Annalen der Physik">Annalen der Physik</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1901_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1901-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SdDhS_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-SdDhS-80">[78]</a></sup> On 30 April 1905 Einstein completed his dissertation, <i>A New Determination of Molecular Dimensions</i><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"_81-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"-81'>[79]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner" title="Alfred Kleiner">Alfred Kleiner</a>, serving as <i><a href="/wiki/Pro_forma" title="Pro forma">pro-forma</a></i> advisor.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"_81-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"-81'>[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"_82-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"-82'>[80]</a></sup> His thesis was accepted in July 1905, and Einstein was awarded a PhD on 15 January 1906.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"_81-2'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"-81'>[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"_82-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"-82'>[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 1905, which has been called Einstein's <i><a href="/wiki/Annus_mirabilis" title="Annus mirabilis">annus mirabilis</a></i> (amazing year), he published <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers">four groundbreaking papers</a>, on the photoelectric effect, <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equivalence_of_mass_and_energy" title="Equivalence of mass and energy">equivalence of mass and energy</a>, which were to bring him to the notice of the academic world, at the age of 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_career">Academic career</span></h3>
<p>By 1908, he was recognized as a leading scientist and was appointed lecturer at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bern" title="University of Bern">University of Bern</a>. The following year, after he gave a lecture on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrodynamics" title="Electrodynamics">electrodynamics</a> and the relativity principle at the University of Zurich, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner" title="Alfred Kleiner">Alfred Kleiner</a> recommended him to the faculty for a newly created professorship in theoretical physics. Einstein was appointed associate professor in 1909.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bG2yp_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-bG2yp-85">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein became a full professor at the German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles-Ferdinand_University" title="Charles-Ferdinand University">Charles-Ferdinand University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> in April 1911, accepting <a href="/wiki/Cisleithania" title="Cisleithania">Austrian</a> citizenship in the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007164_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007164-86">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itl8r_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Itl8r-87">[85]</a></sup> During his Prague stay, he wrote 11 scientific works, five of them on radiation mathematics and on the quantum theory of solids.
</p><p>In July 1912, he returned to his alma mater in Zürich. From 1912 until 1914, he was a professor of theoretical physics at the <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">ETH Zurich</a>, where he taught analytical mechanics and <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">thermodynamics</a>. He also studied <a href="/wiki/Continuum_mechanics" title="Continuum mechanics">continuum mechanics</a>, the molecular theory of heat, and the problem of gravitation, on which he worked with mathematician and friend <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann" title="Marcel Grossmann">Marcel Grossmann</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hXQin_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-hXQin-88">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the "<a href="/wiki/Manifesto_of_the_Ninety-Three" title="Manifesto of the Ninety-Three">Manifesto of the Ninety-Three</a>" was published in October 1914—a document signed by a host of prominent German intellectuals that justified Germany's militarism and position during the First World War—Einstein was one of the few German intellectuals to rebut its contents and sign the pacifistic "<a href="/wiki/Manifesto_to_the_Europeans" title="Manifesto to the Europeans">Manifesto to the Europeans</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScheideler2002333_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScheideler2002333-89">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="761" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png/220px-19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png/330px-19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png/440px-19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:19191125_A_New_Physics_Based_on_Einstein_-_The_New_York_Times.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The New York Times</i> reported confirmation of "the Einstein theory" (specifically, the bending of light by gravitation) based on 29 May 1919 eclipse observations in <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Príncipe">Príncipe</a> (Africa) and <a href="/wiki/Sobral,_Cear%C3%A1" title="Sobral, Ceará">Sobral</a> (Brazil), after the findings were presented on 6 November 1919 to a joint meeting in London of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Astronomical_Society" title="Royal Astronomical Society">Royal Astronomical Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes_19191125_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes_19191125-90">[88]</a></sup> (<a class="external text" href="https://timesmachine.nytimes.com/timesmachine/1919/11/25/96868705.html?pageNumber=17" rel="nofollow">Full text</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>In the spring of 1913, Einstein was enticed to move to Berlin with an offer that included membership in the Prussian Academy of Sciences, and a linked University of Berlin professorship, enabling him to concentrate exclusively on research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-dh-57">[55]</a></sup> On 3 July 1913, he became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Prussian Academy of Sciences">Prussian Academy of Sciences</a> in Berlin. <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck" title="Max Planck">Max Planck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walther_Nernst" title="Walther Nernst">Walther Nernst</a> visited him the next week in Zurich to persuade him to join the academy, additionally offering him the post of director at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Institute_for_Physics" title="Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics">Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics</a>, which was soon to be established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534-91">[89]</a></sup> Membership in the academy included paid salary and professorship without teaching duties at <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a>. He was officially elected to the academy on 24 July, and he moved to Berlin the following year. His decision to move to Berlin was also influenced by the prospect of living near his cousin Elsa, with whom he had started a romantic affair. Einstein assumed his position with the academy, and Berlin University,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> after moving into his <a href="/wiki/Dahlem_(Berlin)" title="Dahlem (Berlin)">Dahlem</a> apartment on 1 April 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-dh-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinstein201518–19_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinstein201518–19-93">[91]</a></sup> As World War I broke out that year, the plan for Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics was delayed. The institute was established on 1 October 1917, with Einstein as its director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EXcH6_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-EXcH6-94">[92]</a></sup> In 1916, Einstein was elected president of the <a href="/wiki/German_Physical_Society" title="German Physical Society">German Physical Society</a> (1916–1918).<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPR19_"Timeline",_p._xix]_95-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceLipscombe2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5eWh2O_3OAQCpgPR19_"Timeline",_p._xix]-95'>[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1911, Einstein used his 1907 <a href="/wiki/Equivalence_principle" title="Equivalence principle">Equivalence principle</a> to calculate the deflection of <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_lens" title="Gravitational lens">light from another star</a> by the Sun's gravity. In 1913, Einstein improved upon those calculations by using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riemannian_space-time" title="Riemannian space-time">Riemannian space-time</a> to represent the gravity field. By the fall of 1915, Einstein had successfully completed his general theory of relativity, which he used to calculate that deflection, and the <a href="/wiki/Tests_of_general_relativity#Perihelion_precession_of_Mercury" title="Tests of general relativity">perihelion precession of Mercury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-dh-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> In 1919, that deflection prediction was confirmed by Sir <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Eddington" title="Arthur Eddington">Arthur Eddington</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_29_May_1919" title="Solar eclipse of 29 May 1919">solar eclipse of 29 May 1919</a>. Those observations were published in the international media, making Einstein world-famous. On 7 November 1919, the leading British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> printed a banner headline that read: "Revolution in Science – New Theory of the Universe – Newtonian Ideas Overthrown".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eddington_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eddington-97">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1920, he became a Foreign Member of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences">Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3gcYy_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-3gcYy-98">[96]</a></sup> In 1922, he was awarded the 1921 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> "for his services to Theoretical Physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the photoelectric effect".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-13">[12]</a></sup> While the <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general theory of relativity</a> was still considered somewhat controversial, the citation also does not treat even the cited photoelectric work as an <i>explanation</i> but merely as a <i>discovery of the law</i>, as the idea of photons was considered outlandish and did not receive universal acceptance until the 1924 derivation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planck_spectrum" title="Planck spectrum">Planck spectrum</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._N._Bose" title="S. N. Bose">S. N. Bose</a>. Einstein was elected a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_1921" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 1921">Foreign Member of the Royal Society (ForMemRS) in 1921</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-frs-4">[3]</a></sup> He also received the <a href="/wiki/Copley_Medal" title="Copley Medal">Copley Medal</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> in 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-frs-4">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein resigned from the Prussian Academy in March 1933. Einstein's scientific accomplishments while in Berlin, included finishing the general theory of relativity, proving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Einstein-de_Haas_effect" title="Einstein-de Haas effect">gyromagnetic effect</a>, contributing to the quantum theory of radiation, and <a href="/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_statistics" title="Bose–Einstein statistics">Bose–Einstein statistics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dh_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-dh-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1921.E2.80.931922:_Travels_abroad"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1921–1922:_Travels_abroad">1921–1922: Travels abroad</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg"><img alt="Einstein, looking relaxed and holding a pipe, stands next to a smiling, well-dressed Elsa who is wearing a fancy hat and fur wrap. She is looking at him." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1038" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/220px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/330px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/440px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Einstein with his second wife, Elsa, in 1921</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_(Nobel).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="280" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png/170px-Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png/255px-Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_(Nobel).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Einstein's official portrait after receiving the 1921 Nobel Prize in Physics</div></div></div>
<p>Einstein visited New York City for the first time on 2 April 1921, where he received an official welcome by Mayor <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Hylan" title="John Francis Hylan">John Francis Hylan</a>, followed by three weeks of lectures and receptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> He went on to deliver several lectures at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>, and in Washington, he accompanied representatives of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> on a visit to the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>. On his return to Europe he was the guest of the British statesman and philosopher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viscount_Haldane" title="Viscount Haldane">Viscount Haldane</a> in London, where he met several renowned scientific, intellectual, and political figures, and delivered a lecture at <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King's College London">King's College London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffmann1972145–148_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffmann1972145–148-100">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997499–508_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997499–508-101">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>He also published an essay, "My First Impression of the U.S.A.", in July 1921, in which he tried briefly to describe some characteristics of Americans, much as had <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville" title="Alexis de Tocqueville">Alexis de Tocqueville</a>, who published his own impressions in <i><a href="/wiki/Democracy_in_America" title="Democracy in America">Democracy in America</a></i> (1835).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7gwHd_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-7gwHd-102">[100]</a></sup> For some of his observations, Einstein was clearly surprised: "What strikes a visitor is the joyous, positive attitude to life ... The American is friendly, self-confident, optimistic, and without envy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolton198420_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolton198420-103">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1922, his travels took him to Asia and later to Palestine, as part of a six-month excursion and speaking tour, as he visited Singapore, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a> and Japan, where he gave a series of lectures to thousands of Japanese. After his first public lecture, he met the emperor and empress at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace" title="Tokyo Imperial Palace">Imperial Palace</a>, where thousands came to watch. In a letter to his sons, he described his impression of the Japanese as being modest, intelligent, considerate, and having a true feel for art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307–308_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307–308-104">[102]</a></sup> In his own travel diaries from his 1922–23 visit to Asia, he expresses some views on the Chinese, Japanese and Indian people, which have been described as xenophobic and racist judgments when they were rediscovered in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38YkY_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-38YkY-105">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because of Einstein's travels to the Far East, he was unable to personally accept the Nobel Prize for Physics at the Stockholm award ceremony in December 1922. In his place, the banquet speech was made by a German diplomat, who praised Einstein not only as a scientist but also as an international peacemaker and activist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxak7_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxak7-107">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>On his return voyage, he visited <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a> for 12 days, his only visit to that region. He was greeted as if he were a head of state, rather than a physicist, which included a cannon salute upon arriving at the home of the British high commissioner, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Herbert_Samuel" title="Sir Herbert Samuel">Sir Herbert Samuel</a>. During one reception, the building was stormed by people who wanted to see and hear him. In Einstein's talk to the audience, he expressed happiness that the Jewish people were beginning to be recognized as a force in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007308_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007308-108">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>Einstein visited Spain for two weeks in 1923, where he briefly met <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal" title="Santiago Ramón y Cajal">Santiago Ramón y Cajal</a> and also received a diploma from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_XIII_of_Spain" title="Alfonso XIII of Spain">King Alfonso XIII</a> naming him a member of the Spanish Academy of Sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-w74nv_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-w74nv-109">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5008" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-220px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-330px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-440px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein at a session of the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation" title="International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation">International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation</a> (<a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>) of which he was a member from 1922 to 1932</div></div></div>
<p>From 1922 to 1932, Einstein was a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation" title="International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation">International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> (with a few months of interruption in 1923–1924),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Q5hgx_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Q5hgx-110">[108]</a></sup> a body created to promote international exchange between scientists, researchers, teachers, artists, and intellectuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vNNnX_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-vNNnX-111">[109]</a></sup> Originally slated to serve as the Swiss delegate, Secretary-General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eric_Drummond" title="Eric Drummond">Eric Drummond</a> was persuaded by Catholic activists <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Halecki" title="Oskar Halecki">Oskar Halecki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Motta" title="Giuseppe Motta">Giuseppe Motta</a> to instead have him become the German delegate, thus allowing <a href="/wiki/Gonzague_de_Reynold" title="Gonzague de Reynold">Gonzague de Reynold</a> to take the Swiss spot, from which he promoted traditionalist Catholic values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e9Xyh_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-e9Xyh-112">[110]</a></sup> Einstein's former physics professor <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">Hendrik Lorentz</a> and the Polish chemist <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Marie Curie</a> were also members of the committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1925:_Visit_to_South_America">1925: Visit to South America</span></h3>
<p>In the months of March and April 1925, Einstein visited South America, where he spent about a month in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, a week in <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>, and a week in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro,_Brazil" title="Rio de Janeiro, Brazil">Rio de Janeiro, Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Einstein's visit was initiated by Jorge Duclout (1856–1927) and Mauricio Nirenstein (1877–1935)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> with the support of several Argentine scholars, including <a href="/wiki/Julio_Rey_Pastor" title="Julio Rey Pastor">Julio Rey Pastor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Laub" title="Jakob Laub">Jakob Laub</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Lugones" title="Leopoldo Lugones">Leopoldo Lugones</a>. The visit by Einstein and his wife was financed primarily by the Council of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Buenos_Aires" title="University of Buenos Aires">University of Buenos Aires</a> and the <i>Asociación Hebraica Argentina</i> (Argentine Hebraic Association) with a smaller contribution from the Argentine-Germanic Cultural Institution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1930.E2.80.931931:_Travel_to_the_US"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1930–1931:_Travel_to_the_US">1930–1931: Travel to the US</span></h3>
<p>In December 1930, Einstein visited America for the second time, originally intended as a two-month working visit as a research fellow at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a>. After the national attention he received during his first trip to the US, he and his arrangers aimed to protect his privacy. Although swamped with telegrams and invitations to receive awards or speak publicly, he declined them all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007368_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007368-117">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>After arriving in New York City, Einstein was taken to various places and events, including <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown</a>, a lunch with the editors of <i>The New York Times</i>, and a performance of <i>Carmen</i> at the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">Metropolitan Opera</a>, where he was cheered by the audience on his arrival. During the days following, he was given the keys to the city by Mayor <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Walker" title="Jimmy Walker">Jimmy Walker</a> and met the president of Columbia University, who described Einstein as "the ruling monarch of the mind".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-118">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Emerson_Fosdick" title="Harry Emerson Fosdick">Harry Emerson Fosdick</a>, pastor at New York's <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Church" title="Riverside Church">Riverside Church</a>, gave Einstein a tour of the church and showed him a full-size statue that the church made of Einstein, standing at the entrance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-118">[116]</a></sup> Also during his stay in New York, he joined a crowd of 15,000 people at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden_(1925)" title="Madison Square Garden (1925)">Madison Square Garden</a> during a <a href="/wiki/Hanukkah" title="Hanukkah">Hanukkah</a> celebration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-118">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="1138" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein (left) and <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="Hollywood, Los Angeles">Hollywood</a> premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">City Lights</a></i>, January 1931</div></div></div>
<p>Einstein next traveled to California, where he met <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caltech" title="Caltech">Caltech</a> president and Nobel laureate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_A._Millikan" title="Robert A. Millikan">Robert A. Millikan</a>. His friendship with Millikan was "awkward", as Millikan "had a penchant for patriotic militarism", where Einstein was a pronounced <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007373_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007373-119">[117]</a></sup> During an address to Caltech's students, Einstein noted that science was often inclined to do more harm than good.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-120">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>This aversion to war also led Einstein to befriend author <a href="/wiki/Upton_Sinclair" title="Upton Sinclair">Upton Sinclair</a> and film star <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a>, both noted for their pacifism. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Laemmle" title="Carl Laemmle">Carl Laemmle</a>, head of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a>, gave Einstein a tour of his studio and introduced him to Chaplin. They had an instant rapport, with Chaplin inviting Einstein and his wife, Elsa, to his home for dinner. Chaplin said Einstein's outward persona, calm and gentle, seemed to conceal a "highly emotional temperament", from which came his "extraordinary intellectual energy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964320_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964320-121">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>Chaplin's film, <i><a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">City Lights</a></i>, was to premiere a few days later in Hollywood, and Chaplin invited Einstein and Elsa to join him as his special guests. <a href="/wiki/Walter_Isaacson" title="Walter Isaacson">Walter Isaacson</a>, Einstein's biographer, described this as "one of the most memorable scenes in the new era of celebrity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-120">[118]</a></sup> Chaplin visited Einstein at his home on a later trip to Berlin and recalled his "modest little flat" and the piano at which he had begun writing his theory. Chaplin speculated that it was "possibly used as kindling wood by the Nazis".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964322_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChaplin1964322-122">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1933:_Emigration_to_the_US">1933: Emigration to the US</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-cartoon1.jpg"><img alt='Cartoon of Einstein, who has shed his "Pacifism" wings, standing next to a pillar labeled "World Peace". He is rolling up his sleeves and holding a sword labeled "Preparedness".' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="624" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/170px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/255px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/340px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-cartoon1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cartoon of Einstein after shedding his "pacifism" wings (<a href="/wiki/Charles_R._Macauley" title="Charles R. Macauley">Charles R. Macauley</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1933</span>)</div></div></div>
<p>In February 1933, while on a visit to the United States, Einstein knew he could not return to Germany with the rise to power of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazis</a> under Germany's new chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997659_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997659-123">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007404_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007404-124">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>While at American universities in early 1933, he undertook his third two-month visiting professorship at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a> in Pasadena. In February and March 1933, the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> repeatedly raided his family's apartment in Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> He and his wife Elsa returned to Europe in March, and during the trip, they learned that the German Reichstag had passed the <a href="/wiki/Enabling_Act_of_1933" title="Enabling Act of 1933">Enabling Act</a> on 23 March, transforming Hitler's government into a <i>de facto</i> legal dictatorship, and that they would not be able to proceed to Berlin. Later on, they heard that their cottage had been raided by the Nazis and Einstein's personal sailboat confiscated. Upon landing in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, Belgium on 28 March, Einstein immediately went to the German consulate and surrendered his passport, formally renouncing his German citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410-126">[124]</a></sup> The Nazis later sold his boat and converted his cottage into a <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">Hitler Youth</a> camp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-el4GB_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-el4GB-127">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugee_status">Refugee status</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_landing_card_(5706142737).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="909" data-file-width="1391" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/220px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/330px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/440px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_landing_card_(5706142737).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Albert Einstein's landing card (26 May 1933), when he landed in <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">Dover</a> (United Kingdom) from <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a> (Belgium) to visit <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a></div></div></div>
